For the latter, the following tags are automatically added to\\n33:  * all metrics registered: {@code config} set to either {@code key.deserializer} or {@code value.deserializer},\\n34:  * and {@code class} set to the deserializer class name.\\n35:  *\\n36:  * @param <T> Type to be deserialized into.\\n37:  */\\n38: public interface Deserializer<T> extends Closeable {\\n39: \\n40:     /**\\n41:      * Configure this class.\\n42:      *\\n43:      * @param configs\\n44:      *        configs in key/value pairs\\n45:      * @param isKey\\n46:      *        whether the deserializer is used for the key or the value\\n47:      */\\n48:     default void configure(Map<String, ?> configs, boolean isKey) {\\n49:         // intentionally left blank\\n50:     }\\n51: \\n52:     /**\\n53:      * Deserialize a record value from a byte array into a value or object.\\n54:      *\\n55:      * <p>It is recommended to deserialize a {@code null} byte array to a {@code null} object.\\n56:      *\\n57:      * @param topic\\n58:      *        topic associated with the data\\n59:      * @param data\\n60:      *        serialized bytes; org.apache.flink.metrics.groups.SourceReaderMetricGroup;\\n28: \\n29: import java.util.Collection;\\n30: import java.util.List;\\n31: import java.util.concurrent.CompletableFuture;\\n32: \\n33: /**\\n34:  * The interface for a source reader which is responsible for reading the records from the source\\n35:  * splits assigned by {@link SplitEnumerator}.\\n36:  *\\n37:  * <p>For most non-trivial source reader, it is recommended to use {@link\\n38:  * org.apache.flink.connector.base.source.reader.SourceReaderBase SourceReaderBase} which provides\\n39:  * an efficient hand-over protocol to avoid blocking I/O inside the task thread and supports various\\n40:  * split-threading models.\\n41:  *\\n42:  * <p>Implementations can provide the following metrics:\\n43:  *\\n44:  * <ul>\\n45:  *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInCounter()} (highly recommended)\\n46:  *   <li>{@link OperatorIOMetricGroup#getNumBytesInCounter()} (recommended)\\n47:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#getNumRecordsInErrorsCounter()} (recommended)\\n48:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingRecordsGauge(Gauge)}\\n49:  *   <li>{@link SourceReaderMetricGroup#setPendingBytesGauge(Gauge)}\\n50:  * </ul>\\n51:  *\\n52:  * @param <T> The type of the record emitted by this source reader.\\n53:  * @param <SplitT> The type of the source splits.\\n54:  */\\n55: @Public\\n56: public interface SourceReader<T, SplitT extends SourceSplit>\\n57:         extends AutoCloseable, CheckpointListener {\\n58: \\n59:     /** Start the reader. */\\n60:     void start();\\n61: \\n62:     /**\\n63:      * Poll the next available record into the {@link ReaderOutput}.\\n64:      *\\n65:      * <p>The implementation must make sure this method is non-blocking.\\n66:      *\\n67:      * <p>Although the implementation can emit multiple records into the given ReaderOutput, it is\\n68:      * recommended not doing so. Instead, emit one record into the ReaderOutput and return a {@link\\n69:      * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE} to let the caller thread know there are more records available.\\n70:      *\\n71:      * @return The InputStatus of the SourceReader after the method invocation.\\n72:      */\\n73:     InputStatus pollNext(ReaderOutput<T> output) throws Exception;\\n74: \\n75:     /**\\n76:      * Checkpoint on the state of the source.\\n77:      *\\n78:      * @return the state of the source.\\n79:      */\\n80:     List<SplitT> snapshotState(long checkpointId);\\n81: \\n82:     /**\\n83:      * Returns a future that signals that data is available from the reader.\\n84:      *\\n85:      * <p>Once the future completes, the runtime will keep calling the {@link\\n86:      * #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} method until that method returns a status other than {@link\\n87:      * InputStatus#MORE_AVAILABLE}. After that, the runtime will again call this method to obtain\\n88:      * the next future. Once that completes, it will again call {@link #pollNext(ReaderOutput)} and\\n89:      * so on.\\n90:      *\\n91:      * <p>The contract is the following: If the reader has data available, then all futures\\n92:      * previously returned by this method must eventually complete. Otherwise the source might stall\\n93:      * indefinitely.\\n94:      *\\n95:      * <p>It is not a problem to have occasional \\\"false positives\\\", meaning to complete a future\\n96:      * even if no data is available. However, one should not use an \\\"always complete\\\" future in\\n97:      * cases no data is available, because that will result in busy waiting loops calling {@code\\n98:      * pollNext(...)} even though no data is available.\\n99:      *\\n100:      * @return a future that will be completed once there is a record available to poll.\\n101:      */\\n102:     CompletableFuture<Void> isAvailable();\\n103: \\n104:     /**\\n105:      * Adds a list of splits for this reader to read. This method is called when the enumerator\\n106:      * assigns a split via {@link SplitEnumeratorContext#assignSplit(SourceSplit, int)} or {@link\\n107:      * SplitEnumeratorContext#assignSplits(SplitsAssignment)}.\\n108:      *\\n109:      * @param splits The splits assigned by the split enumerator.\\n110:      */\\n111:     void addSplits(List<SplitT> splits);\\n112: \\n113:     /**\\n114:      * This method is called when the reader is notified that it will not receive any further\\n115:      * splits.\\n116:      *\\n117:      * <p>It is triggered when the enumerator calls {@link\\n118:      * SplitEnumeratorContext#signalNoMoreSplits(int)} with the reader's parallel subtask.\\n119:      */\\n120:     void notifyNoMoreSplits();\\n121: \\n122:     /**\\n123:      * Handle a custom source event sent by the {@link SplitEnumerator}. This method is called when\\n124:      * the enumerator sends an event via {@link SplitEnumeratorContext#sendEventToSourceReader(int,\\n125:      * SourceEvent)}.\\n126:      *\\n127:      * <p>This method has a default implementation that does nothing, because most sources do not\\n128:      * require any custom events.\\n129:      *\\n130:      * @param sourceEvent the event sent by the {@link SplitEnumerator}.\\n131:      */\\n132:     default void handleSourceEvents(SourceEvent sourceEvent) {}\\n133: \\n134:     /**\\n135:      * We have an empty default implementation here because most source readers do not have to\\n136:      * implement the method.\\n137:      *\\n138:      * @see CheckpointListener#notifyCheckpointComplete(long)\\n139:      */\\n140:     @Override\\n141:     default void notifyCheckpointComplete(long checkpointId) throws Exception {}\\n142: \\n143:     /**\\n144:      * Pauses or resumes reading of individual source splits.\\n145:      *\\n146:      * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so updating subscriptions can be\\n147:      * done atomically. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs the\\n148:      * opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\\n149:      *\\n150:      * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\\n151:      * and the source reads from more than one split.\\n152:      *\\n153:      * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\\n154:      * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\\n155:      * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\\n156:      *\\n157:      * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\\n158:      * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\\n159:      */\\n160:     @PublicEvolving\\n161:     default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\\n162:             Collection<String> splitsToPause, Collection<String> splitsToResume) {\\n163:         throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\\n164:                 \\\"This source reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\\\n\\\"\\n165:                         + \\\"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\\\n\\\"\\n166:                         + \\\"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\\\n\\\"\\n167:                         + \\\"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\\\n\\\"\\n168:                         + \\\"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\\\n\\\"\\n169:                         + \\\"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\\\n\\\"\\n170:                         + \\\"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\\\");\\n171:     }\\n172: }\\n173: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc@de39c3e1777c43fe3363b3fd7784bf46b57a99c2/-/blob/flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/connector/source/SourceReader.java\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"569a3a6b-7f5d-45c9-8214-45e5be9e81a6","uuid":"b0cdad96-3ad0-4a91-a09a-2d1555b30ced","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one\\n3:  * or more contributor license agreements. The implementation could either read from a single split\\n30:  * or from multiple splits.\\n31:  *\\n32:  * @param <E> the element type.\\n33:  * @param <SplitT> the split type.\\n34:  */\\n35: @PublicEvolving\\n36: public interface SplitReader<E, SplitT extends SourceSplit> extends AutoCloseable {\\n37: \\n38:     /**\\n39:      * Fetch elements into the blocking queue for the given splits. The fetch call could be blocking\\n40:      * but it should get unblocked when {@link #wakeUp()} is invoked. In that case, the\\n41:      * implementation may either decide to return without throwing an exception, or it can just\\n42:      * throw an interrupted exception. In either case, this method should be reentrant, meaning that\\n43:      * the next fetch call should just resume from where the last fetch call was waken up or\\n44:      * interrupted. It is up to the implementer to either read all the records of the split or to\\n45:      * stop reading them at some point (for example when a given threshold is exceeded). In that\\n46:      * later case, when fetch is called again, the reading should restart at the record where it\\n47:      * left off based on the {@code SplitState}.\\n48:      *\\n49:      * @return the Ids of the finished splits.\\n50:      * @throws IOException when encountered IO errors, such as deserialization failures.\\n51:      */\\n52:     RecordsWithSplitIds<E> fetch() throws IOException;\\n53: \\n54:     /**\\n55:      * Handle the split changes. This call should be non-blocking.\\n56:      *\\n57:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if an invalid split is added to\\n58:      * the reader (for example splits without any records), it should be put back into {@link\\n59:      * RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up\\n60:      * resources created for it.\\n61:      *\\n62:      * <p>For the consistency of internal state in SourceReaderBase, if a split is removed, it\\n63:      * should be put back into {@link RecordsWithSplitIds} as finished splits so that\\n64:      * SourceReaderBase could be able to clean up resources created for it.\\n65:      *\\n66:      * @param splitsChanges the split changes that the SplitReader needs to handle.\\n67:      */\\n68:     void handleSplitsChanges(SplitsChange<SplitT> splitsChanges);\\n69: \\n70:     /** Wake up the split reader in case the fetcher thread is blocking in {@link #fetch()}. */\\n71:     void wakeUp();\\n72: \\n73:     /**\\n74:      * Pauses or resumes reading of individual splits readers.\\n75:      *\\n76:      * <p>Note that no other methods can be called in parallel, so it's fine to non-atomically\\n77:      * update subscriptions. This method is simply providing connectors with more expressive APIs\\n78:      * the opportunity to update all subscriptions at once.\\n79:      *\\n80:      * <p>This is currently used to align the watermarks of splits, if watermark alignment is used\\n81:      * and the source reads from more than one split.\\n82:      *\\n83:      * <p>The default implementation throws an {@link UnsupportedOperationException} where the\\n84:      * default implementation will be removed in future releases. To be compatible with future\\n85:      * releases, it is recommended to implement this method and override the default implementation.\\n86:      *\\n87:      * @param splitsToPause the splits to pause\\n88:      * @param splitsToResume the splits to resume\\n89:      */\\n90:     default void pauseOrResumeSplits(\\n91:             Collection<SplitT> splitsToPause, Collection<SplitT> splitsToResume) {\\n92:         throw new UnsupportedOperationException(\\n93:                 \\\"This split reader does not support pausing or resuming splits which can lead to unaligned splits.\\\\n\\\"\\n94:                         + \\\"Unaligned splits are splits where the output watermarks of the splits have diverged more than the allowed limit.\\\\n\\\"\\n95:                         + \\\"It is highly discouraged to use unaligned source splits, as this leads to unpredictable\\\\n\\\"\\n96:                         + \\\"watermark alignment if there is more than a single split per reader. It is recommended to implement pausing splits\\\\n\\\"\\n97:                         + \\\"for this source. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\\\n\\\"\\n98:                         + \\\"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\\\n\\\"\\n99:                         + \\\"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\\\");\\n100:     }\\n101: }\\n102: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc@de39c3e1777c43fe3363b3fd7784bf46b57a99c2/-/blob/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"569a3a6b-7f5d-45c9-8214-45e5be9e81a6","uuid":"27f1bab8-830f-4204-aef2-5dcf02602d82","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one\\n3:  * or more contributor license agreements. At your own risk, you can allow unaligned source splits by setting the\\n\"\n98:                         + \"configuration parameter `pipeline.watermark-alignment.allow-unaligned-source-splits' to true.\\n\"\n99:                         + \"Beware that this configuration parameter will be dropped in a future Flink release.\");\n100:     }\n101: }\n102: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc@de39c3e1777c43fe3363b3fd7784bf46b57a99c2/-/blob/flink-connectors/flink-connector-base/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/connector/base/source/reader/splitreader/SplitReader.java"}}}

import java.util.regex.Pattern;\n49: \n50: import static org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils.propsToMap;\n51: \n52: /**\n53:  * A client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster.\n54:  * <p>\n55:  * This client transparently handles the failure of Kafka brokers, and transparently adapts as topic partitions\n56:  * it fetches migrate within the cluster. This client also interacts with the broker to allow groups of\n57:  * consumers to load balance consumption using <a href=\"#consumergroups\">consumer groups</a>.\n58:  * <p>\n59:  * The consumer maintains TCP connections to the necessary brokers to fetch data.\n60:  * Failure to close the consumer after use will leak these connections.\n61:  * The consumer is not thread-safe. See <a href=\"#multithreaded\">Multi-threaded Processing</a> for more details.\n62:  *\n63:  * <h3>Cross-Version Compatibility</h3>\n64:  * This client can communicate with brokers that are version 0.10.0 or newer. Older or newer brokers may not support\n65:  * certain features. For example, 0.10.0 brokers do not support offsetsForTimes, because this feature was added\n66:  * in version 0.10.1. You will receive an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}\n67:  * when invoking an API that is not available on the running broker version.\n68:  * <p>\n69:  *\n70:  * <h3>Offsets and Consumer Position</h3>\n71:  * Kafka maintains a numerical offset for each record in a partition. This offset acts as a unique identifier of\n72:  * a record within that partition, and also denotes the position of the consumer in the partition. For example, a consumer\n73:  * which is at position 5 has consumed records with offsets 0 through 4 and will next receive the record with offset 5.\n74:  * Note that offsets are not guaranteed to be consecutive (such as compacted topic or when records have been produced\n75:  * using transactions). For example, if the consumer did read a record with offset 4, but 5 is not an offset\n76:  * with a record, its position might advance to 6 (or higher) directly. Similarly, if the consumer's position is 5,\n77:  * but there is no record with offset 5, the consumer will return the record with the next higher offset.\n78:  * There are actually two notions of position relevant to the user of the consumer:\n79:  * <p>\n80:  * The {@link #position(TopicPartition) position} of the consumer gives the offset of the next record that will be given\n81:  * out. It will be one larger than the highest offset the consumer has seen in that partition. It automatically advances\n82:  * every time the consumer receives messages in a call to {@link #poll(Duration)}.\n83:  * <p>\n84:  * The {@link #commitSync() committed position} is the last offset that has been stored securely. Should the\n85:  * process fail and restart, this is the offset that the consumer will recover to. The consumer can either automatically commit\n86:  * offsets periodically; or it can choose to control this committed position manually by calling one of the commit APIs\n87:  * (e.g. {@link #commitSync() commitSync} and {@link #commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback) commitAsync}).\n88:  * <p>\n89:  * This distinction gives the consumer control over when a record is considered consumed. It is discussed in further\n90:  * detail below.\n91:  *\n92:  * <h3><a name=\"consumergroups\">Consumer Groups and Topic Subscriptions</a></h3>\n93:  *\n94:  * Kafka uses the concept of <i>consumer groups</i> to allow a pool of processes to divide the work of consuming and\n95:  * processing records. These processes can either be running on the same machine or they can be\n96:  * distributed over many machines to provide scalability and fault tolerance for processing. All consumer instances\n97:  * sharing the same {@code group.id} will be part of the same consumer group.\n98:  * <p>\n99:  * Each consumer in a group can dynamically set the list of topics it wants to subscribe to through one of the\n100:  * {@link #subscribe(Collection, ConsumerRebalanceListener) subscribe} APIs. Kafka will deliver each message in the\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java%3FL1-100"}}}

Let me also check the SerializationSchema file and the Kafka consumer's internals to understand the Fetcher thread. Let me also look for the KafkaProducer send method to understand how Serializer is used.\n\nNow I have enough context to write the full analysis. Let me write it to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.\n\nKey findings:\n1. **Kafka Producer side**:\n   - `Producer<K,V>` interface (Producer.java) - top-level API with `send(ProducerRecord<K,V>)`, `flush()`, transactional methods\n   - `KafkaProducer` implements Producer and uses `Serializer<K>` and `Serializer<V>` to convert key/value objects to bytes before sending\n   - `ProducerRecord<K,V>` wraps the topic, partition, timestamp, headers, key, and value being sent\n   - `Serializer<T>` interface provides the conversion logic from objects to byte arrays\n\n2. **Kafka Consumer side**:\n   - `Consumer<K,V>` interface (Consumer.java) - provides `poll(Duration)`, `commitSync()`, and offset management methods\n   - `KafkaConsumer` implements Consumer and uses `Deserializer<K>` and `Deserializer<V>` to convert bytes back to objects\n   - `ConsumerRecord<K,V>` contains the received topic, partition, offset, timestamp, headers, key, and value\n   - `OffsetAndMetadata` wraps the offset along with leaderEpoch and metadata\n   - `Deserializer<T>` interface converts byte arrays back to typed objects\n\n3. **Flink Source API** (`flink-core`):\n   - `Source<T, SplitT, EnumChkT>` interface acts as a factory for creating SourceReader, SplitEnumerator, and serializers, with methods like `getBoundedness()` and `create`\n\nDefining the SourceReader and SplitEnumerator interfaces...\n\nThe connector-base framework provides concrete implementations like `SourceReaderBase` which manages split fetching through background threads and queues records for emission, along with `SplitReader` for fetching raw data and `RecordEmitter` for transforming elements into the desired output format.\n\nFlink's serialization layer handles converting between Kafka bytes and domain objects through `DeserializationSchema` and `SerializationSchema`, while the runtime layer wraps everything in a `SourceOperator` that integrates with Flink's checkpoint machinery.\n\nWhen a checkpoint is triggered, the `SourceOperator` captures the current state from the source reader, which for Kafka includes the split offsets, and when the checkpoint completes, it notifies the reader so the Kafka connector can commit those offsets back to the broker.\n\nThere's also a dual serialization layer at play: Kafka's own deserializers convert raw bytes into `ConsumerRecord` objects, while Flink's `DeserializationSchema` then transforms those records into the domain objects that flow through the pipeline.\n\nThe threading model separates concerns nicely—Kafka's internal fetcher and sender threads handle the network layer, while Flink wraps this with `SplitFetcher` background threads that poll from the consumer and queue results, which the main task thread then consumes through integrates with Flink's checkpoint machinery; `snapshotState()` at line 608 and `notifyCheckpointComplete()` at line 640\n\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Kafka Producer Path\n```\nApplication object T\n  -> Serializer<K>.serialize(topic, key)      [bytes for key]\n  -> Serializer<V>.serialize(topic, value)    [bytes for value]\n  -> ProducerRecord<K,V>(topic, partition, timestamp, key, value, headers)\n  -> Producer<K,V>.send(ProducerRecord)\n  -> KafkaProducer [RecordAccumulator batches, Sender thread sends to broker]\n```\n\n### 2. Kafka Consumer Path\n```\nKafkaConsumer.poll(Duration)\n  -> Fetcher/ConsumerDelegate fetches byte records from broker\n  -> Deserializer<K>.deserialize(topic, keyBytes)    [typed key]\n  -> Deserializer<V>.deserialize(topic, valueBytes)  [typed value]\n  -> ConsumerRecord<K,V>(topic, partition, offset, timestamp, key, value, headers)\n  -> ConsumerRecords<K,V> returned to caller\n  -> KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)  [at checkpoint]\n```\n\n### 3. Flink Source API (flink-core)\n```\nSource<T, SplitT, EnumChkT>\n  -> createEnumerator(SplitEnumeratorContext)  -> SplitEnumerator<SplitT, CheckpointT>\n  -> createReader(SourceReaderContext)          -> SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n  -> getSplitSerializer()                       -> SimpleVersionedSerializer<SplitT>\n  -> getEnumeratorCheckpointSerializer()        -> SimpleVersionedSerializer<EnumChkT>\n\nSplitEnumerator\n  -> discovers topic partitions, assigns them as splits to SourceReaders\n  -> snapshotState(checkpointId): saves partition assignment state\n\nSourceReader\n  -> addSplits(List<SplitT>): receives assigned partitions\n  -> pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>): emits records to downstream\n  -> snapshotState(checkpointId): returns current split states (with offsets)\n  -> notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId): triggers Kafka offset commit\n```\n\n### 4. Flink Connector-Base Framework (flink-connector-base)\n```\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT> implements SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n  |\n  +-- SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT>\n  |     +-- SplitFetcher threads (background)\n  |           +-- SplitReader<E, SplitT>  (wraps KafkaConsumer.poll())\n  |                 fetch() -> RecordsWithSplitIds<E>  (E = ConsumerRecord<byte[],byte[]>)\n  |\n  +-- FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>  (handoff queue)\n  |\n  +-- RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>\n        emitRecord(ConsumerRecord, SourceOutput<T>, splitState)\n          -> DeserializationSchema<T>.deserialize(valueBytes) -> T\n          -> output.collect(record)\n```\n\n### 5. Flink Serde Boundary\n```\nKafka layer (within KafkaConsumer):\n  byte[] -> Deserializer<K/V> -> ConsumerRecord<K,V>\n\nFlink layer (within RecordEmitter / KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema):\n  ConsumerRecord<byte[],byte[]> -> DeserializationSchema<T> -> T (Flink domain object)\n\nKafka sink layer:\n  T -> SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T) -> byte[] -> ProducerRecord -> KafkaProducer\n```\n\n### 6. Checkpoint-Offset Integration\n```\nFlink Checkpoint Trigger\n  -> SourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext)          [SourceOperator.java:608]\n       -> readerState.update(sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId))\n       -> SourceReaderBase.snapshotState(checkpointId)           [SourceReaderBase.java:348]\n            -> collects KafkaSplit states (each containing current TopicPartition + offset)\n            -> serializes splits into ListState<byte[]> via SimpleVersionedSerializer\n\nFlink Checkpoint Completion\n  -> SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)       [SourceOperator.java:640]\n       -> sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n       -> [Kafka connector's SourceReader override]\n            -> KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n               [commits exactly the offsets captured at snapshotState time]\n```\n\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How Kafka's Consumer API is Wrapped by Flink's SplitReader\n\nThe Flink Kafka connector (built on top of this repo's `flink-connector-base` framework) implements the `SplitReader<ConsumerRecord<byte[],byte[]>, KafkaPartitionSplit>` interface. Each `KafkaPartitionSplit` represents one Kafka `TopicPartition` with a start offset and optional stop offset.\n\nThe `SplitFetcherManager` creates background `SplitFetcher` threads; each thread repeatedly calls `SplitReader.fetch()`. Inside the Kafka-connector's SplitReader, this translates to `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration)`. The resulting `ConsumerRecord<byte[],byte[]>` objects are batched into `RecordsWithSplitIds` and enqueued into the shared `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue`.\n\nThe main Flink task thread runs `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()`, which drains records from this queue, calls `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()` for each record, and forwards them to the `SourceOutput<T>`.\n\n### The Dual Serialization Boundary\n\nThere are two distinct deserialization layers:\n\n**Layer 1 — Kafka's Deserializer** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Deserializer.java`): This runs inside `KafkaConsumer` and converts the raw broker bytes into typed key/value Java objects. In the Flink Kafka connector, the consumer is typically configured with `ByteArrayDeserializer` for both key and value, deliberately keeping data as `byte[]` and deferring domain conversion to Flink.\n\n**Layer 2 — Flink's DeserializationSchema** (`flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/serialization/DeserializationSchema.java`): This runs inside `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()` in the Flink task thread. It receives the raw `byte[]` value (and optionally headers, topic, partition) from the `ConsumerRecord` and produces the final domain object `T`. The `DeserializationSchema` interface contracts:\n- `T deserialize(byte[] message)` — simple single-record conversion\n- `void deserialize(byte[] message, Collector<T> out)` — supports one-to-many expansion\n- `boolean isEndOfStream(T nextElement)` — signals bounded source termination\n- `TypeInformation<T> getProducedType()` — enables Flink type system integration\n\nFor the **sink direction**, `SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T element)` converts the Flink domain object to `byte[]`, which is then wrapped in a `ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>` sent via `KafkaProducer`.\n\n### Checkpoint Completion Triggers Kafka Offset Commits\n\nFlink's exactly-once source semantics integrate with Kafka's consumer group offset tracking through a two-phase protocol:\n\n1. **Snapshot phase**: When Flink triggers a checkpoint, `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` (line 608) calls `sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)`. The Kafka connector's SourceReader returns a list of `KafkaPartitionSplit` objects, each embedding the current consumed-but-not-yet-committed offset for its `TopicPartition`. These splits are serialized and stored in Flink's managed operator state (`ListState<byte[]>`). At this point, Kafka offsets have **not** been committed to the broker yet.\n\n2. **Completion phase**: Once the checkpoint barrier has propagated through the entire DAG and all operators have persisted their state, the JobManager notifies all operators via `notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)`. `SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete()` (line 640) delegates to `sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)`, which in the Kafka connector calls `KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)` with the offsets captured during the snapshot phase.\n\nThis design guarantees **at-least-once** delivery by default, and **exactly-once** when combined with Flink's transactional sinks: Kafka offsets are only committed after Flink has durably checkpointed the processing state, so a failure before checkpoint completion causes re-consumption from the last committed offset.\n\n### Consumer Group Coordination Model\n\nKafka's consumer group protocol (coordinated by the group coordinator broker) assigns `TopicPartition`s to individual consumer instances. In the Flink integration, the `SplitEnumerator` running in the JobManager takes ownership of partition discovery and assignment, bypassing Kafka's built-in group rebalancing for the per-partition assignment step. Each Flink source subtask operates its own `KafkaConsumer` instance with `group.id` set, subscribing to specific partitions via `KafkaConsumer.assign()` (not `subscribe()`). This gives Flink full control over partition-to-subtask mapping and makes rebalancing deterministic (driven by Flink's SplitEnumerator snapshot/restore, not Kafka's rebalance protocol).\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Kafka side**:\n- `KafkaProducer` uses a background `Sender` thread that drains the `RecordAccumulator` (batch buffer) and sends `ProduceRequest`s over the network.\n- `KafkaConsumer` uses an internal `Fetcher` component (or `ConsumerDelegate` in newer versions) that issues `FetchRequest`s; the consumer itself is single-threaded and not thread-safe.\n\n**Flink side**:\n- `SplitFetcherManager` creates one or more `SplitFetcher` threads. Each thread runs a loop calling `SplitReader.fetch()` (which internally calls `KafkaConsumer.poll()`), then enqueues results into `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue`.\n- The main Flink task thread (mailbox thread) calls `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()`, consumes from the queue via the future-based handoff protocol, invokes `RecordEmitter`, and emits to `SourceOutput<T>`.\n- This threading model ensures that the blocking `KafkaConsumer.poll()` never blocks the Flink task mailbox thread, while the `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue` uses `CompletableFuture` completion to wake the task thread when data is available.\n\n\n## Summary\n\nStreaming data flows from Kafka brokers through Flink by wrapping `KafkaConsumer.poll()` inside Flink's `SplitReader` abstraction, which runs in a background `SplitFetcher` thread managed by `SplitFetcherManager`; raw `ConsumerRecord<byte[],byte[]>` objects are handed off via a `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue` to the main task thread, where `RecordEmitter` applies Flink's `DeserializationSchema` to produce typed domain objects for downstream operators. The checkpoint-offset integration is two-phased: at checkpoint time, `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` captures current partition offsets in Flink managed state without committing to Kafka, and only upon checkpoint completion does `notifyCheckpointComplete()` trigger `KafkaConsumer.commitSync()`, ensuring offsets are advanced in Kafka only when Flink has durably persisted the corresponding processing state. There is a dual serialization boundary — Kafka's own `Deserializer<T>` (kept as passthrough `ByteArrayDeserializer`) and Flink's `DeserializationSchema<T>` — giving operators control over byte-level format interpretation independent of the Kafka wire protocol.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2080,"cache_read_input_tokens":84536,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2080,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"569a3a6b-7f5d-45c9-8214-45e5be9e81a6","uuid":"e75079c4-2f2e-43dd-953f-8cef4a45a6b7"}
